It can conduct basic, all-in-one health check-ups from the comfort of your own dwelling or office &#8212; and connect with your doctor remotely.</p>\n<p>TytoHome is an electronic, portable, at-home exam kit plus smart-phone app &#8212; that lets you perform guided medical tests with a health-care provider. You can conduct exams on the heart, lungs, abdomen, ears, throat, skin, and body temperature. You can see and hear your physician using the device. Results appear instantly on your physician&#8217;s screen.</p>\n<p>Then you can receive a diagnosis, a treatment plan, and prescriptions &#8212; anytime + anywhere. TytoHome helps your physician quickly, conveniently diagnose common conditions like: ear infection, head cold, sore throat, fever, cough, sinus + chest congestion, stomach ache, bug bites, and rashes.</p>\n<p>To use TytoHome all you need is a smart-phone or tablet &#8212; plus a wi-fi internet connection. You can record your exam and send it to your doctor, or conduct a live exam guided by your physician.</p>\n<p>And if you need a doctor, TytoCare has a trusted physicians network available 24 hours a day / 365 days a year &#8212; for expert help. resource &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>Financial products built on modern technology (called fin-tech) &#8212; especially start-ups that improve on  old-fashioned institutions such as banking + insurance &#8212; are sweeping the world. The new consumer + small business offerings are available as web apps on laptops, smart-phones, and tablets. They promise:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>better agility</li>\n<li>better service speed</li>\n<li>better convenience</li>\n<li>better focused products + services</li>\n<li>better look + feel</li>\n<li>better mobility</li>\n<li>better prices</li>\n<li>better account management</li>\n<li>better customer comfort</li>\n<li>better customer education</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Insurance is considered one of the most antiquated financial industries &#8212; burdened by too many hands-on processes that should + could be automated, with sluggish performance from legacy software + out-dated computer systems.</p>\n<p>But it&#8217;s finally experiencing a major renovation. Innovations from fin-tech are re-inventing insurance. 1000s of start-ups have launched contemporary products for every corner of a customer&#8217;s insurance needs. class=\"pastel full\">\n<colgroup>\n<col style=\"width: 30%;\" />\n<col /> </colgroup>\n<thead>\n<tr>\n<th style=\"text-align: left;\" scope=\"col\" height=\"14\"></th>\n<th style=\"text-align: left;\" scope=\"col\"></th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td>topic</td>\n<td>progress in bio-medicine</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>story</td>\n<td>Medical artificial intelligence software detects aneurysms.</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; facts &#8212;-</span><em></em></p>\n<p><em>an artificial intelligence software tool found aneurysms better than physicians:</em></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">part 1:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li>computer software called artificial intelligence (AI) specializes in revealing patterns in large + complex piles of data</li>\n<li>AI programs can often pick-out key issues, better than a person</li>\n<li>the software is trained to sift through mountains of info &#8212; efficiently sorting data into maps of knowledge</li>\n<li>so AI is especially useful in fields that process high volumes of data &#8212; like: medicine, economics, physics, engineering</li>\n<li>medical researchers hope to build AI software that can diagnose patients</li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">part 2:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li>a team at Stanford Univ. built an AI tool to help detect brain aneurysms in people</li>\n<li>a brain aneurysm is a bulge in a blood vessel in the brain<strong></strong></li>\n<li>aneurysms are dangerous because they can leak or rupture &#8212; causing bleeding into the brain</li>\n<li>usually an aneurysm forms because a blood vessel is weak</li>\n<li>so early detection + diagnosis are important to avoid patient death or disability</li>\n<li>each year: 30,000 people in the US suffer a ruptured brain aneurysm</li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">part 3:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li>the team&#8217;s AI software tool highlights areas of a brain scan that are likely to contain an aneurysm</li>\n<li>it successfully found 6 more aneurysms than physicians did &#8212; in a set of 100 brain scans</li>\n<li>to find aneurysms in a patient, physicians comb through 100s of brain images</li>\n<li>aneurysms come in many sizes + shapes &#8212; and balloon-out at tricky angles</li>\n<li>some appear as tiny blips on brain scan images</li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">part 4.</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li>the team taught their software by showing it 611 3D brain scans &#8212; where they outlined actual aneurysms</li>\n<li>so the software learned how to identify what an aneurysm looks like in high detail</li>\n<li>to use the tool, the team feeds the software a 3D brain scan made with the imaging technique called CT</li>\n<li>CT stands for computed tomography angiogram &#8212; it creates a map of body tissues + blood vessels</li>\n<li>then the AI software overlays the CT image with a colored highlight, wherever it finds an aneurysm</li>\n<li>the team envisions an updated AI program designed to find aneurysms after they&#8217;ve burst</li>\n</ul>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img style=' A high-tech helmet to prevent sports brain injury","link":"https://www.kurzweilai.net/?p=333519","description":"<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft size-full wp-image-334384 noshadow\" title=\"art - football player + ink dot - no. 1\" src=\"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/art-football-player-+-ink-dot-no.-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"663\" /></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; in this post &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>~ story<br />\n~ by the numbers<br />\n~ featurettes<br />\n~ pages<br />\n~ reading<br />\n~ watching</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; story &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>The <a href=\"https://www.nfl.com\" target=\"_blank\">National Football League</a> (NFL) is asking inventors, scientists, physicians, and engineers to make the game of football safer. 300 of the brightest minds from around the world gathered at a <a href=\"https://www.playsmartplaysafe.com/nfl-helmet-challenge-symposium\" target=\"_blank\">symposium</a> to talk about changes that could be made &#8212; one of the key improvements will be a better helmet design.</p>\n<p>The NFL&#8217;s initiative &#8212; called <a href=\"https://www.playsmartplaysafe.com/headhealthtech\" target=\"_blank\">Head Health Tech</a> &#8212; set aside $3 million in grants to support development of new helmet prototypes. The goal of the NFL <a href=\"https://www.playsmartplaysafe.com/nfl-helmet-challenge\" target=\"_blank\">helmet challenge</a> is preventing traumatic head injury to players through innovation. The science teams are exploring:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>advanced modeling software &#8212; to see how injuries happen, test wearable gear</li>\n<li>improved helmet design &#8212; to protect the skull, neck, and brain</li>\n<li>composite materials &#8212; to construct better gear that can absorb + withstand crushing impact</li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">Injuries are a mounting concern.</span></p>\n<p>Traumatic brain and spine injuries &#8212; such as concussion, whiplash, fractured skull, and broken neck bones &#8212; have been an increasing concern for football players from youth to adult. These injuries affect both amateur and professional leagues. Head trauma from impact shock can lead to life-long disability and even death. In the 100 years since popular football became an all-time American contact-sport, few improvements have been made to the safety gear that makes-up a standard football uniform.</p>\n<p>The NFL said: “We see opportunities to change the paradigm of how helmets are designed &#8212; and use the world&#8217;s state-of-the-art from multiple fields. There are new approaches, new materials, new concepts.”</p>\n<p>This is the league’s first helmet challenge. The winner of the contest will be awarded $1 million and also $2 million in grant funding to develop the prototype. The first round of proposals are due January 2020 &#8212; and final helmet prototypes are due May 2021.</p>\n<p>Year 2020 marks the NFL&#8217;s 100th game season &#8212; and public scrutiny is intensifying, while legal teams and families demand that players be better protected from concussion. A team of neuro-scientists at a start-up called <a href=\"https://www.brainguard.com\" target=\"_blank\">BrainGuard</a> are working quickly to develop a better helmet that can prevent brain injuries.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft size-full wp-image-334252 noshadow\" title=\"art - better helmet - no. 7\" src=\"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/art-better-helmet-no.-7.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"785\" /></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">image</span> | above<br />\n<em> The NFL&#8217;s helmet challenge is part of their Head Health Tech initiative.</em></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">art:</span> by <a href=\"https://www.NFL.com\" target=\"_blank\">NFL</a></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">Designing for shock absorption.</span></p>\n<p>Pressure from the new football season &#8212; and continued heart-breaking accounts from NFL players who suffered severe brain injuries &#8212; makes the roll-out of a better helmet increasingly urgent.</p>\n<p>BrainGuard thinks its design could be a game-changer. Their <a href=\"https://www.brainguard.com/science-team\" target=\"_blank\">team of engineers</a>, led by neuro-scientist Robert Knight MD, bashes a prototype football helmet from every angle &#8212; hitting it again and again &#8212; to see how it absorbs and disperses energy before the blow impacts the brain.</p>\n<p>The helmet features an inner and outer shell &#8212; connected by highly absorbent padding and a network of rubber struts that stretch, acting as shock absorbers. No matter where the helmet is hit, only the outer shell moves.</p>\n<p>Knight explained: “Every time it does that, and it moves, these struts are absorbing some of the force &#8212; mitigating the amount of force that goes to the inner shell, which then of course goes directly to your skull and to your brain.”</p>\n<p>The design specifically addresses rotational force injuries: the twisting and turning of the brain caused by severe blows to the head. When tested against other helmets, BrainGuard says the amount of rotational force was reduced by 25 % &#8212; 45 %.</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">Life-threatening second impact syndrome.</span></p>\n<p>The medical condition called <a href=\"http://headwayfoundation.com/concussions\" target=\"_blank\">second impact syndrome</a> is a potentially catastrophic injury that occurs when a person &#8212; who already has a concussion &#8212; sustains a second head injury, before symptoms from the first concussion have healed. Concussion causes brain inflammation. If the patient sustains a second head injury during this vulnerable time, the brain can swell so much there isn’t enough space in the skull &#8212; this can destroy brain tissue. And in some cases lead to death.</p>\n<p>Improved helmets must be designed to prevent the player from sustaining a concussion at all. Current helmets don&#8217;t provide protection from extreme impact, rotational forces, or the cumulative effect of multiple collisions.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft size-full wp-image-333873 noshadow\" title=\"photo - better helmet + model - no. 1\" src=\"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/photo-better-helmet-+-model-no.-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"588\" /></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">image</span> | above<br />\n<em>Prototype of a helmet that absorbs shock + rotational forces.</em></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">photo:</span> by <a href=\"https://www.BrainGuard.com\" target=\"_blank\">BrainGuard</a></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">A need for new standards.</span></p>\n<p>Football players&#8217; parents and coaches welcome any safety improvements. The helmet is a critical piece of gear, like airbags in motor vehicles. And the same way airbags are now required by law in all automobiles, BrainGuard hopes its 2-shelled helmets will become standard equipment &#8212; not just for football players: but also for hockey, baseball, and cycling. Any sport or activity where a better helmet could reduce brain injuries.</p>\n<p>The NFL has 1,700 players. But there are 1.2 million youth each year playing <a href=\"https://www.popwarner.com\" target=\"_blank\">Pop Warner</a> football, and <a href=\"https://www.maxpreps.com\" target=\"_blank\">high school</a> + <a href=\"https://www.espn.com/college-football\" target=\"_blank\">college</a> football &#8212; who are equally at risk for head injury. 63,000 high school students in the United States suffer a traumatic brain injury per year, leaving many kids with persistent long-term physical + cognitive disability.</p>\n<p>The World Health Organization predicts that traumatic brain injury will become a leading cause of death + disability in the world by year 2020.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft  wp-image-334401 noshadow\" title=\"photo - football player + boy - no. 6\" src=\"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/photo-football-player-+-boy-no.-6.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"466\" /></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft size-full wp-image-334405 noshadow\" title=\"photo - football field + helmet - no. 5\" src=\"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/photo-football-field-+-helmet-no.-5.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"466\" /></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">featurette</span> | watch</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">group:</span> by Univ. of California + BrainGuard<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">featurette title:</span> Building a better helmet</p>\n<p><iframe frameborder=\"0\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/389229537\" width=\"640\" webkitallowfullscreen mozallowfullscreen allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">featurette</span> | watch</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">group:</span> by Univ. of Washington + Vicis<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">featurette title:</span> Building a better helmet</p>\n<p><iframe frameborder=\"0\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/389196785\" width=\"640\" webkitallowfullscreen mozallowfullscreen allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img style=' float: right; padding: 4px; margin: 0 0 2px 7px;'  class=\"wp-image-334406 noshadow alignright\" title=\"everyday - calculator + table - no. 4\" src=\"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/everyday-calculator-+-table-no.-4.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"424\" height=\"651\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\"> &#8212; by the numbers &#8212;</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">statistics:</span> by CDC<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">source:</span> <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/mmwr/volumes/66/ss/ss6609a1.htm\" target=\"_blank\">data</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; from traumatic brain injury<br />\n&#8212; over a period of 1 year</p>\n<ul>\n<li>2.5 million emergency room visits</li>\n<li>56,000 deaths</li>\n<li>282,000 hospitalizations</li>\n</ul>\n<p>* <em>not including military activities</em><br />\n* <em>for year 2013</em></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">featurette</span> | watch</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">group:</span> by CDC<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">featurette title:</span> What is a concussion?</p>\n<p><iframe frameborder=\"0\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/389197095\" width=\"640\" webkitallowfullscreen mozallowfullscreen allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft  wp-image-333882 noshadow\" title=\"story - brand - Heads Up - by CDC - no. 1\" src=\"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/story-brand-Heads-Up-by-CDC-no.-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"332\" height=\"332\" /><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">on the web</span> | pages</p>\n<p>CDC | <a href=\"http://www.cdc.gov\" target=\"_blank\">home</a><br />\nCDC | <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/headsup/index.html\" target=\"_blank\">Heads-Up</a><br />\nCDC | <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/headsup/helmets/index.html\" target=\"_blank\">helmet safety</a></p>\n<p>Heads-Up by CDC is an education pack about safe sports and activities for kids + teens.</p>\n<p>The materials teach prevention, recognition, and response to head concussion and other serious brain injuries.</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">tag line:</span> saving lives + protecting people</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img class=\"wp-image-333631 noshadow \" title=\"story - brand - Centers for Disease Control and Prevention - no. 1\" src=\"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/story-brand-Centers-for-Disease-Control-and-Prevention-no.-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"542\" /></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">Hope for BrainGuard&#8217;s prototype helmet.</span></p>\n<p>The helmet designed by BrainGuard has layers that move to protect the head.</p>\n<p>BrainGuard has been awarded 13 United States patents + 6 foreign patents. Their innovative, multi-layered helmet protects against rotational shear forces that are a major contributor to traumatic brain injury (TBI). These damaging forces also play a role in the brain&#8217;s accumulation of toxic, malformed proteins seen in chronic traumatic encephalopathy (CTE) &#8212; a brain disease that forms from repetitive head blows.</p>\n<p>Encephalopathy is a medical term meaning: brain disease, damage, or malfunction. <strong></strong>It has a wide range of symptoms</p>\n<ul>\n<li>mild &#8212; such as memory loss or personality changes</li>\n<li>severe &#8212; such as dementia, seizures, coma, or death.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>CTE is consistently found in people who&#8217;ve suffered multiple traumatic brain injuries &#8212; from accidents, sports, or military experiences. BrainGuard&#8217;s helmet design solution results in marked rotational force reduction in lab testing. The hope for the improved helmet is that is can prevent concussion.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p>IMAGE</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">featurette</span> | watch</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">group:</span> by Associated Press<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">series:</span> <a href=\"https://apnews.com/ScienceSays\" target=\"_blank\">Science Says</a><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">featurette title:</span> How repeated head blows affect the brain</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">tag line:</span> The definitive source for news.</p>\n<p><iframe frameborder=\"0\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/389197004\" width=\"640\" webkitallowfullscreen mozallowfullscreen allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; summary &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>The medical term CTE stands for chronic traumatic encephalopathy. Researchers are tackling fresh questions about this long-term degenerative brain disease now that it has been detected in the brains of nearly 200 football players after death. As a new NFL season gets underway, here’s a look at what’s known about CTE.</p>\n<p>We examine the evidence behind health + science claims by putting them into context. in this post &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>~ story<br />\n~ by the numbers<br />\n~ report<br />\n~ pages</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; story &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>To keep-up with modern times and stay relevant to today&#8217;s marketplace: enterprise must adopt, support, and integrate high-level computing that&#8217;s networked, maintained, and distributed across all areas of business. The companies + organizations that fall behind in the arena of info-tech (information technology or IT) risk their bottom line, and risk losing the best employees to more leading-edge groups who are up-to-date with digital infra-strcuture.</p>\n<p>In a world that&#8217;s primarily focused on the computerization of processes, record keeping, inventory, management, and production &#8212; any enterprise that lags in IT will become an industry dinosaur.</p>\n<p>Implementing new digital tools &#8212; and upgrading antique legacy computer systems and non-digital practices &#8212; can be a huge task. Incumbent businesses the slowest to change. According to top research firm <a href=\"https://www.mckinsey.com/\" target=\"_blank\">McKinsey</a> &#8212; a startling 70% of digital transformation programs fail because of:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>lack of employee engagement</li>\n<li>inadequate management support</li>\n<li>lack of accountability</li>\n<li>low levels of collaboration</li>\n</ul>\n<p>IT personnel are in the best position to cope with these kinds of challenges &#8212; but often lack the support they need to begin and maintain crucial IT infrastructure projects.</p>\n<p>A recent report from <a href=\"https://www.workfront.com/\" target=\"_blank\">WorkFront</a> &#8212; a project management and software services company &#8212; examines 5 common stumbling blocks faced by info-tech professionals trying to achieve digital transformation. facts &#8212;-</span></p>\n<p><em>researchers crafted an electronic glove that&#8217;s worn over a prosthetic hand, providing sense perception:</em></p>\n<ul>\n<li>advances in flexible + stretchable electronics are making breakthroughs in prosthetics</li>\n<li>the prototype for this e-glove was made by Purdue University engineers</li>\n</ul>\n<ul>\n<li>the e-glove &#8212; gives amputees with prosthetic limbs a sense of touch</li>\n<li>the e-glove &#8212; mimics the sensory capabilities of a human limb in its own unique way</li>\n<li>the e-glove &#8212; fits over existing prosthetic hands in a range of shapes + sizes, giving them new capability</li>\n<li>the e-glove &#8212; fits seamlessly on top of any hand shape</li>\n<li>the e-glove &#8212; is fitted with a suite of flexible electronic sensors</li>\n<li>the e-glove &#8212; is finished in soft rubber to mimic the look + feel of a human hand</li>\n<li>the e-glove &#8212; has life-like: softness, appearance, warmth</li>\n</ul>\n<ul>\n<li>the e-glove&#8217;s sensors detect: pressure, temperature, hydration, bio-signals &#8212; of whatever it touches</li>\n<li>that data is collected + relayed to a connected wrist-watch</li>\n<li>the wrist-watch &#8212; displays the readings in real-time</li>\n<li>the wrist-watch &#8212; also passes the data wirelessly to a separate device for processing</li>\n</ul>\n<ul>\n<li>in the next stage of development: the e-glove will provide feedback to the wearer</li>\n<li>examples of feedback are: audio cues + tactile vibration</li>\n</ul>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img style=' float: left; This campaign is a commitment to growth, innovation, and discovery.</p>\n<p>This research in advancing human prosthetics, aligns with Purdue&#8217;s Giant Leaps celebration of the university’s global progress in health &#8212; part of Purdue’s 150th anniversary. #ffaa00;\">&#8212; 4 themes &#8212;</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li>giant leaps | space &#8212; <em>Earth • exploration • economics</em></li>\n<li>giant leaps | AI • algorithms • automation &#8212; <em>balancing humanity + tech</em></li>\n<li>giant leaps | sustainable economy + planet &#8212; <em>innovate today for tomorrow</em></li>\n<li>giant leaps | health + longevity &#8212; <em>quality of life</em></li>\n</ul>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft  wp-image-326200 noshadow\" title=\"everyday - play button - no. 3\" web</span> | pages</p>\n<p>Purdue Univ. | <a href=\"https://www.purdue.edu\" target=\"_blank\">home</a><br />\nPurdue Univ. | <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/user/PurdueUniversity\" target=\"_blank\">YouTube channel</a></p>\n<p>Purdue Univ. | Giant Leaps: <a href=\"https://takegiantleaps.com/\" target=\"_blank\">home</a><br />\nPurdue Univ. | Giant Leaps: <a href=\"https://takegiantleaps.com/ideas-festival\" target=\"_blank\">Ideas Festival</a></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; notes &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>e-glove <em></em>= electronic glove<br />\nAI = artificial intelligence</p>\n<hr />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">[ story file ]</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">story title:</span> making headlines | e-Glove&#8217;s flexible sensors give prosthetic hands a sense of touch<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">deck:</span> topic: progress in electronics<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">year:</span> 2019<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\"><br />\nfolder:</span> stories on progress</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">[ end of file ]</span></p>\n","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 25 Oct 2019 05:00:07 +0000","feedId":11321,"bgimg":"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/photo-e-glove-for-prosthetics-no.-1.png","linkMd5":"0d572e2fc77a300c1911e300d3706fb2","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn89@2020_6/2020/08/25/01-22-13-511_0a29c0044f60f785.webp","destWidth":1500,"destHeight":750,"sourceBytes":913230,"destBytes":75440,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/photo-e-glove-for-prosthetics-no.-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn89@2020_6/2020/08/25/01-22-13-511_0a29c0044f60f785.webp","https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/everyday-rolled-up-newspaper-no.-4.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn44@2020_6/2020/08/25/01-22-37-378_a1ae9efd115e5b5b.webp","https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/everyday-play-button-no.-3.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn28@2020_4/2020/08/25/01-22-30-567_f72f234d72f63e13.webp","https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/photo-e-glove-for-prosthetics-no.-2.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn95@2020_5/2020/08/25/01-22-36-747_2571504277ac9c90.webp","https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/story-brand-Medium-no.-3.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn0@2020_1/404.jpg","https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/story-brand-Purdue-University-no.-3.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn29@2020_5/2020/08/25/01-22-27-308_bf6c0cd80e809bd0.webp","https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/story-brand-Purdue-University-no.-4.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn55@2020_3/2020/08/25/01-22-29-752_303aace60411e5f9.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598318532657},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:22:12","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:22:12","title":"essay &#124; Testing if artificial intelligence has become self-aware","link":"http://www.kurzweilai.net/?p=303345","description":"<p><img class=\" wp-image-303428 noshadow\" title=\"woman-machine\" src=\"http://www.kurzweilai.net/images/woman-machine.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"960\" height=\"678\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">image </span>| above<br />\n<em>by artist Gerd Altmann</em></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; essay &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>essay title: Testing if artificial intelligence has become self-aware<br />\ndeck:<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">author: </span>by Susan Schneider PhD<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">author:</span> by Edwin Turner PhD<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">date:</span> August 2017</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; introduction &#8212;</span></p>\n<p><em>by Susan Schneider PhD + Edwin Turner PhD</em></p>\n<p>Every moment of your waking life and whenever you dream, you have the distinct inner feeling of being “you.” When you see the warm hues of a sunrise, smell the aroma of morning coffee or mull over a new idea, you are having conscious experience. But could an artificial intelligence (AI) ever have experience, like some of the androids depicted in the TV shows <em>Westworld</em> and <em>Humans</em>, or the synthetic beings in the iconic film <em>Blade Runner</em>?</p>\n<p>The question is not so far-fetched. Robots are currently being developed to work inside nuclear reactors, fight wars and care for the elderly. As AIs grow more sophisticated, they are projected to take over many human jobs within the next few decades. So we must ponder the question: Could AIs develop conscious experience?</p>\n<p>This issue is pressing for several reasons. First, ethicists worry that it would be wrong to force AIs to serve us if they can suffer and feel a range of emotions. Second, consciousness could make AIs volatile or unpredictable, raising safety concerns (or conversely, it could increase an AI’s empathy; based on its own subjective experiences, it might recognize consciousness in us and treat us with compassion).</p>\n<p>Third, machine consciousness could impact the viability of brain-implant technologies, like those to be developed by Elon Musk’s new company, Neuralink. If AI cannot be conscious, then the parts of the brain responsible for consciousness could not be replaced with chips <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=k7M4b_9PJ-g\" target=\"_blank\">without causing a loss of consciousness</a>. And, in a similar vein, a person couldn’t upload their brain to a computer to avoid death, because that upload wouldn’t be a conscious being.</p>\n<p>In addition, if AI eventually out-thinks us yet lacks consciousness, there would still be an important sense in which we humans are superior to machines; it <em>feels</em> like something to be us. But the smartest beings on the planet wouldn’t be conscious or sentient.</p>\n<p>A lot hangs on the issue of machine consciousness, then. Yet neuroscientists are far from understanding the basis of consciousness in the brain, and philosophers are at least equally far from a complete explanation of the nature of consciousness.</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; a test for machine consciousness &#8212;</span><strong><br />\n</strong></p>\n<p>So what can be done? We believe that we do not need to define consciousness formally, understand its philosophical nature or know its neural basis to recognize indications of consciousness in AIs. Each of us can grasp something essential about consciousness, just by introspecting; we can all experience what it feels like, from the inside, to exist.</p>\n<p>Based on this essential characteristic of consciousness, we propose a test for machine consciousness, the AI Consciousness Test (ACT), which looks at whether the synthetic minds we create have an experience-based understanding of the way it feels, from the inside, to be conscious.</p>\n<p>One of the most compelling indications that normally functioning humans experience consciousness, although this is not often noted, is that nearly every adult can <em>quickly</em> and <em>readily </em>grasp concepts based on this quality of felt consciousness. Such ideas include scenarios like minds switching bodies (as in the film <em>Freaky Friday</em>); life after death (including reincarnation); and minds leaving “their” bodies (for example, astral projection or ghosts). Whether or not such scenarios have any reality, they would be exceedingly difficult to comprehend for an entity that had no conscious experience whatsoever. It would be like expecting someone who is completely deaf from birth to appreciate a Bach concerto.</p>\n<p>Thus, the ACT would challenge an AI with a series of increasingly demanding natural language interactions to see how <em>quickly</em> and <em>readily </em>it can grasp and use concepts and scenarios based on the internal experiences we associate with consciousness. At the most elementary level we might simply ask the machine if it conceives of itself as anything other than its physical self.</p>\n<p>At a more advanced level, we might see how it deals with ideas and scenarios such as those mentioned in the previous paragraph. At an advanced level, its ability to reason about and discuss philosophical questions such as “the hard problem of consciousness” would be evaluated. At the most demanding level, we might see if the machine invents and uses such a consciousness-based concept on its own, without relying on human ideas and inputs.</p>\n<p>Consider this example, which illustrates the idea: Suppose we find a planet that has a highly sophisticated silicon-based life form (call them “Zetas”). Scientists observe them and ponder whether they are conscious beings. What would be convincing proof of consciousness in this species? If the Zetas express curiosity about whether there is an afterlife or ponder whether they are more than just their physical bodies, it would be reasonable to judge them conscious. If the Zetas went so far as to pose philosophical questions about consciousness, the case would be stronger still.</p>\n<p>There are also nonverbal behaviors that could indicate Zeta consciousness such as mourning the dead, religious activities or even turning colors in situations that correlate with emotional challenges, as chromatophores do on Earth. Such behaviors could indicate that it feels like something to be a Zeta.</p>\n<p>The death of the mind of the fictional HAL 9000 AI computer in Stanley Kubrick’s <a href=\"https://youtu.be/c8N72t7aScY\"><em>2001: A Space Odyssey</em></a> provides another illustrative example. The machine in this case is not a humanoid robot as in most science fiction depictions of conscious machines; it neither looks nor sounds like a human being (a human did supply HAL&#8217;s voice, but in an eerily flat way). Nevertheless, the <em>content</em> of what it says as it is deactivated by an astronaut &#8212; specifically, a plea to spare it from impending “death” &#8212; conveys a powerful impression that it is a conscious being with a subjective experience of what is happening to it.</p>\n<p>Could such indicators serve to identify conscious AIs on Earth? Here, a potential problem arises. Even today’s robots can be programmed to make convincing utterances about consciousness, and a truly superintelligent machine could perhaps even use information about neurophysiology to infer the presence of consciousness in humans. If sophisticated but non-conscious AIs aim to mislead us into believing that they are conscious for some reason, their knowledge of human consciousness could help them do so.</p>\n<p>We can get around this though. One proposed technique in AI safety involves “boxing in” an AI—making it unable to get information about the world or act outside of a circumscribed domain, that is, the “box.” We could deny the AI access to the internet and indeed prohibit it from gaining any knowledge of the world, especially information about conscious experience and neuroscience.</p>\n<p>Some doubt a superintelligent machine could be boxed in effectively &#8212; it would find a clever escape. We do not anticipate the development of superintelligence over the next decade, however. Furthermore, for an ACT to be effective, the AI need not stay in the box for long, just long enough administer the test.</p>\n<p>ACTs also could be useful for “consciousness engineering” during the development of different kinds of AIs, helping to avoid using conscious machines in unethical ways or to <a href=\"http://cosmos.nautil.us/feature/72/it-may-not-feel-like-anything-to-be-an-alien\">create synthetic consciousness when appropriate</a>.</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; beyond the Turing test &#8212;<strong><br />\n</strong></span></p>\n<p>An ACT resembles Alan Turing’s <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_test\">celebrated test for intelligence</a>, because it is entirely based on behavior &#8212; and, like Turing’s, it could be implemented in a formalized question-and-answer format. (An ACT could also be based on an AI’s behavior or on that of a group of AIs.)</p>\n<p>But an ACT is also quite unlike the Turing test, which was intended to bypass any need to know what was transpiring inside the machine. By contrast, an ACT is intended to do <em>exactly the opposite</em>; it seeks to reveal a subtle and elusive property of the machine’s mind. Indeed, a machine might fail the Turing test because it cannot pass for human, but pass an ACT because it exhibits behavioral indicators of consciousness.</p>\n<p>This is the underlying basis of our ACT proposal. It should be said, however, that the applicability of an ACT is inherently limited. An AI could lack the linguistic or conceptual ability to pass the test, like a nonhuman animal or an infant, yet still be capable of experience. So passing an ACT is <em>sufficient</em> but not <em>necessary</em> evidence for AI consciousness &#8212; although it is the best we can do for now. It is a first step toward making machine consciousness accessible to objective investigations.</p>\n<p>So, back to the superintelligent AI in the “box” &#8212; we watch and wait. Does it begin to philosophize about minds existing in addition to bodies, like Descartes? Does it dream, as in Isaac Asimov’s <em>Robot Dreams</em>? Does it express emotion, like Rachel in <em>Blade Runner</em>?<strong> </strong>Can it readily understand the human concepts that are grounded in our internal conscious experiences, such as those of the soul or atman?</p>\n<p>The age of AI will be a time of soul-searching &#8212; both of ours, and for theirs.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">on the web</span> | pages</p>\n<p>Susan Schneider PhD | <a href=\"http://schneiderwebsite.com/index.html\" target=\"_blank\">home</a></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">bio:</span> teacher | philosophy + cognitive science &#8212; Univ. of Connecticut<br />\nbio: member | Ethics + Technology Group &#8212; Yale Univ.<br />\nbio: member | Institute for Advanced Study &#8212; Princeton Univ.<br />\nbio: researcher | YHouse</p>\n<p>DOTLINE</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">books</span> | by Susan Schneider PhD</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">book:</span> <em>the Language of Thought</em><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">deck:</span> A new philosophical direction<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">author:</span> by Susan Schneider PhD<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">this book on Good Reads</span> | <a href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9674882-the-language-of-thought\" target=\"_blank\">visit</a></p>\n<p>book: <em>Science Fiction + Philosophy</em><br />\ndeck: From time travel to super-intelligence<br />\nauthor: by Susan Schneider PhD<br />\nthis book on Good Reads | visit</p>\n<p>book: <em>the Blackwell Companion to Consciousness</em><br />\ndeck:<br />\nauthor: by Susan Schneider PhD<br />\nthis book on Good Reads | visit</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">on the web</span> | pages</p>\n<p>Elvin L. The film shows the Apollo 11 astronauts conducting several tasks during extra-vehicular activity (EVA) operations on the moon&#8217;s surface. The EVA lasted 2.5 hours.</p>\n<p>The Apollo 11 EVA began at 10:40 pm (Eastern time) on July 20, 1969 &#8212; when astronaut Neil Armstrong exited from the craft first. While descending to the moon, he released the Modularized Equipment Stowage Assembly on the lunar module&#8217;s descent stage.</p>\n<p>A video camera on this module provided live television coverage of humanity&#8217;s first step on Earth&#8217;s moon. On their only EVA the astronauts had many tasks to do &#8212; in a short time. During this first visit to the moon, the astronauts:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>remained within 100 meters of the lunar module</li>\n<li>collected 47 pounds of samples</li>\n<li>deployed 4 experiments</li>\n<li>they completed all the steps successfully</li>\n</ul>\n<p>After spending 2 hours + 30 minutes on the moon&#8217;s surface &#8212; the astronauts ended the EVA at 1:12 am (Eastern time) on July 21, 1969.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft size-full wp-image-330805 noshadow\" title=\"everyday - style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; book &#8212;</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">book title:</span> <em>the Square and the Tower</em><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">deck:</span> Networks + Power: from the Freemasons to Facebook<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">author:</span> by Niall Ferguson<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">year:</span> 2018</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">this book on Good Reads</span> | visit</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; summary &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>A re-casting of the turning points in world history, including the one we&#8217;re living through, as a collision between old power hierarchies and new social networks.</p>\n<p>Most history is hierarchical: it&#8217;s about emperors, presidents, prime ministers and field marshals. It&#8217;s about states, armies and corporations. It&#8217;s about orders from on high. Even history &#8220;from below&#8221; is often about trade unions and workers&#8217; parties. But what if that&#8217;s simply because hierarchical institutions create the archives that historians rely on? What if we are missing the informal, less well documented social networks that are the true sources of power and drivers of change?</p>\n<p>The 21st century has been hailed as the Age of Networks. However, in <em>the Square and the Tower</em>, Niall Ferguson argues that networks have always been with us, from the structure of the brain to the food chain, from the family tree to freemasonry. Throughout history, hierarchies housed in high towers have claimed to rule, but often real power has resided in the networks in the town square below. For it is networks that tend to innovate. And it is through networks that revolutionary ideas can contagiously spread. Just because conspiracy theorists like to fantasize about such networks doesn&#8217;t mean they are not real.</p>\n<p>From the cults of ancient Rome to the dynasties of the Renaissance, from the founding fathers to Facebook, <em>the Square and the Tower</em> tells the story of the rise, fall and rise of networks, and shows how network theory&#8211;concepts such as clustering, degrees of separation, weak ties, contagions and phase transitions&#8211;can transform our understanding of both the past and the present.</p>\n<p>Just as <em>The Ascent of Money</em> put Wall Street into historical perspective, so <em>The Square and the Tower</em> does the same for Silicon Valley. And it offers a bold prediction about which hierarchies will withstand this latest wave of network disruption&#8211;and which will be toppled.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p>on the web | pages</p>\n<p>Niall Ferguson | home</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 10 Jan 2020 06:00:29 +0000","feedId":11321,"bgimg":"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/the-square-and-the-tower-cover-140x212.jpg","linkMd5":"83cf2359fd67e72ecc6efdcda81a3591","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn93@2020_4/2020/08/25/01-22-38-619_665f4a5e013778bf.webp","destWidth":140,"destHeight":212,"sourceBytes":10824,"destBytes":5920,"author":"","publishedOrCreatedDate":1598318532655},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:22:12","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:22:12","title":"event &#124; Researchers use AI to model millions of drug combination side effects","link":"http://www.kurzweilai.net/?p=318320","description":"<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft  wp-image-337370 noshadow\" title=\"photo - pills + orange - no. 1\" src=\"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/photo-pills-+-orange-no.-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"466\" /></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; in this post &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>~ story<br />\n~ by definition<br />\n~ by the numbers<br />\n~ reading</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; story &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>Millions of people take approx. 5 or more medications a day &#8212; but testing the many side-effects of those pharmaceutical drug combinations has historically been difficult. Researchers at Stanford Univ. have invented a way to predict side-effects using computer modeling based-on artificial intelligence. The team explained that most drug combinations (called poly-pharmacy) have never been systematically studied.</p>\n<p>Their AI software system is called <a href=\"http://snap.stanford.edu/decagon\" target=\"_blank\">Decagon</a> &#8212; and they say it can help physicians make better decisions about what drugs to prescribe. It could also help researchers find better combinations of prescription drugs to treat complex diseases.</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">Limited knowledge.</span></p>\n<p>With so many prescription drugs currently on the pharmaceutical market: “it’s practically impossible to test a new drug in combination with all other drugs &#8212; because just for one drug that would be 5,000 new experiments,” said Marinka Zitnik PhD &#8212; a researcher on the project.</p>\n<p>Zitnik said: &#8220;With some new drug combinations we don’t know what will happen.” The researchers explained that poly-pharmacy side-effects happen because of drug -to- drug interactions &#8212; the effects of one pharmaceutical drug may change (positively or negatively) if it&#8217;s taken with another drug.</p>\n<p>The knowledge of medical drug interactions is often limited &#8212; because the complex relationships between many pharmaceutical combinations is only rarely observed. Discovering poly-pharmacy side-effects is a serious challenge that&#8217;s important for patient health.</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">Tracking how pharmaceutical drugs affect proteins.</span></p>\n<p>The researchers created a data-base containing descriptions of how 19,000+ proteins found in the human body interact with each other &#8212; and how various drugs affect these proteins. Using 4+ million known associations between drugs and their side-effects, the team crafted a method to identify patterns in how side-effects arise &#8212; based-on the way pharmaceutical drugs interact with proteins.</p>\n<p>With that method, the system could predict the outcome of taking 2 drugs together. To evaluate their method, the group looked to see if its predictions came true. In many cases, they did. For example: there was no existing indication that the combination of a cholesterol drug named <a href=\"https://www.lipitor.com\" target=\"_blank\">Lipitor</a> and a blood-pressure medication called <a href=\"https://www.norvasc.com\" target=\"_blank\">Norvasc</a>, could lead to muscle inflammation. But Decagon predicted that it would, and that foresight was <a href=\"https://www.hindawi.com/journals/cricc/2017/3801819/\" target=\"_blank\">proven correct</a>.</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">Looking ahead.</span></p>\n<p>The team hopes to extend their results to include more multiple drug interactions. They aim to create a user-friendly tool &#8212; that gives physicians guidance on whether it’s a good idea to prescribe a particular pharmaceutical drug to a particular patient. And to help researchers developing drug protocols for complex diseases, with fewer side-effects.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">by definition</span> | what is poly-pharmacy?</p>\n<p style=\"padding-left: 30px;\"><strong>pol • y • phar • ma • cy</strong> &#8212; <em>noun</em></p>\n<p style=\"padding-left: 30px;\">&#8212; the simultaneous prescription of multiple pharmaceutical drugs &#8212; to treat a single condition.<br />\n&#8212; the simultaneous use of multiple pharmaceutical drugs by a single patient &#8212; for one or more conditions.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; by the numbers &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>According to the CDC:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>23% of United States citizens take 3+ prescription drugs each month<em></em></li>\n<li>39% of United States citizens over age 65 take 5+ prescription drugs each month</li>\n<li>a number that’s increased 3-fold in the last several decades</li>\n<li>there are approx. 5,000 pharmaceutical drugs on the market &#8212; with approx. 1,000 known side-effects, taken individually</li>\n<li>making approx. 125 billion possible side-effects between all possible pairs of drugs</li>\n<li>Stanford Univ. says most drug combinations have never been systemically studied</li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">source:</span> <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/nchs/fastats/drug-use-therapeutic.htm\" target=\"_blank\">CDC</a></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">on the web</span> | reading</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">group:</span> Stanford Univ.<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">motto:</span> The wind of freedom blows.</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">story:</span> AI helps Stanford Univ. computer scientists predict the side effects of millions of drug combinations<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">read</span> | <a href=\"https://news.stanford.edu/2018/07/10/ai-predicts-drug-pair-side-effects\" target=\"_blank\">story</a></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; summary &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>Millions of people take upwards of 5 medications a day, but testing the side-effects of such combinations is impractical. Now Stanford Univ. computer scientists have figured out how to predict side-effects using artificial intelligence.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">on the web</span> | reading</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">group:</span> Mark Allen Group<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">tag line:</span> text</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">publication:</span> <em>the Engineer</em><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">story:</span> Decagon AI system predicts side-effects of drug combinations<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">read</span> | <a href=\"https://www.theengineer.co.uk/decagon-ai-side-effects-drugs\" target=\"_blank\">story</a></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; summary &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>Stanford Univ. researchers have developed an AI tool called Decagon that can predict the potential side-effects of drug combinations.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; notes &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>AI = artificial intelligence</p>\n<p>CDC = Centers for Disease Control + Prevention • United States<br />\nUS = United States</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">[ post file ]</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">post title:</span> digest | Researchers use AI to model millions of drug combination side effects<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">deck:</span> Solving this historically complex problem.<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">folder:</span> stories on progress</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">[ end of file ]</span></p>\n","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sun, 10 May 2020 05:00:41 +0000","feedId":11321,"bgimg":"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/photo-pills-+-orange-no.-1.png","linkMd5":"3538031e1f481adf3107980b8bad25ec","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn34@2020_1/2020/08/25/01-22-14-534_b8c1fb2302b92a2a.webp","destWidth":5760,"destHeight":3840,"sourceBytes":16130613,"destBytes":136200,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/photo-pills-+-orange-no.-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn34@2020_1/2020/08/25/01-22-14-534_b8c1fb2302b92a2a.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598318532651},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:22:12","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:22:12","title":"digest &#124; Tech teams-up: artificial intelligence for football","link":"https://www.kurzweilai.net/?p=333582","description":"<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft size-full wp-image-334053 noshadow\" title=\"art - football player + geometric - no. 4\" src=\"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/art-football-player-+-geometric-no.-4.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"876\" /></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; in this post &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>~ story<br />\n~ by definition<br />\n~ pages<br />\n~ reading</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212;  story &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>The National Football League (NFL)  is partnering with Amazon&#8217;s high-tech company Amazon Web Services (AWS) to get a deeper understanding of the game of football &#8212; with the goal to better predict + prevent player head injury like concussion.</p>\n<p>The computer software field of artificial intelligence (AI) is transforming every major industry, including sports. Applied to football, AI is improving how player safety is visualized and assessed &#8212; shaping tech that can see how injuries happen.</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">Seeing complex patterns.</span></p>\n<p>Since year 2017, the NFL has officially used Amazon&#8217;s data collection + management tools to build a significant data-base of statistical info &#8212; for better analysis of player performance and game outcomes.</p>\n<p>That ongoing <a href=\"https://nextgenstats.nfl.com\" target=\"_blank\">program</a> &#8212; called <a href=\"https://aws.amazon.com/nfl\" target=\"_blank\">Next Generation Stats</a> &#8212; is expanding to tackle the growing concern of player safety. An enormous amount of data is captured by placing radio frequency identification (RFID) tags on player’s shoulder gear and the game ball. RFID uses electro-magnetic fields to automatically identify + track tags attached to objects. These tags electronically store info. Then ultra-wide-band signal receivers track the players and ball movement down to the inch.</p>\n<p>NFL signed onto a partnership with <a href=\"https://www.zebra.com\" target=\"_blank\">Zebra</a> to install RFID data sensors in players’ shoulder pads, helmets, and across NFL stadiums. These chips detect how fast the player&#8217;s running &#8212; and how heavy an impact is that a player&#8217;s taken, which is important for medically diagnosing trauma to the head.</p>\n<p>Behind every incredible football play are 1000s of data-points that could be missed: such as player’s acceleration, football field location, and movement patterns. The NFL uses Amazon Web Services to track the scale, speed, and complexity of that data &#8212; in real-time.</p>\n<p>So with Amazon&#8217;s machine learning + artificial intelligence &#8212; software tools that can sift through mountains of confusing or overwhelming data, and see key patterns in it &#8212; the NFL can visualize detailed action on the football field. The software uncovers insights, and expands the fan experience with a broad range of stats. The knowledge gained from the data also helps coaches improve game-play.</p>\n<p>The NFL is expanding its partnership with Amazon Web Services &#8212; using Amazon&#8217;s pattern-recognition software and cloud computing products.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p>IMAGE</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">featurette</span> | watch</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">group:</span> NFL + Amazon Web Services<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">featurette title:</span> A team-up to transform player health + safety</p>\n<p><iframe frameborder=\"0\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/389527591\" width=\"640\" webkitallowfullscreen mozallowfullscreen allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">The digital athlete.</span></p>\n<p>The most revolutionary component of the NFL + Amazon partnership is the creation of the Digital Athlete &#8212; a computer simulation model that can replicate infinite scenarios within the game environment.</p>\n<p>The Digital Athlete simulation applies Amazon&#8217;s computer vision tech to the NFL’s data-sets. The data comes from many sources: like player position, play type, equipment choice, playing surface, environmental factors &#8212; and player injury info.</p>\n<p>The knowledge that comes from seeing patterns in the matrix of this data will improve injury treatment. And eventually help predict + prevent injuries in football &#8212; and other sports.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">The future of football.</span></p>\n<p>The expanded partnership combines the NFL’s extensive set of game data with Amazon&#8217;s tech.</p>\n<p><em>the goals:</em></p>\n<ul>\n<li>computer vision models will automatically detect when concussions happen to players</li>\n<li>identify + understand the forces that cause traumatic brain injury</li>\n<li>detect + prevent a wider range of injury, like damage to the lower body</li>\n<li>visualize + understand the many factors at play at the moment of injury</li>\n<li>make changes to the game + gear to protect players</li>\n<li>share knowledge with sports equipment designers + makers</li>\n<li>approach the problem by studying data and bio-mechanics</li>\n</ul>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">The engineering road-map.</span></p>\n<p>The NFL also created the &#8220;engineering road-map.&#8221; It&#8217;s a $60 million initiative to engage teams &#8212; of bio-mechanical + bio-medical + bio-engineering researchers &#8212; that will develop solutions to predict + prevent player injury.</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Player Health + Safety • by NFL | <a href=\"https://www.playsmartplaysafe.com/newsroom/fact-sheets/nfl-engineering-roadmap-fact-sheet\" target=\"_blank\">engineering road-map</a></li>\n<li>Player Health + Safety • by NFL | <a href=\"https://www.playsmartplaysafe.com/newsroom/videos/nfls-engineering-roadmap-driving-progress-toward-better-protective-equipment/\" target=\"_blank\">innovation through collaboration</a></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">A research example.</span></p>\n<p>To better understand how concussion-causing injuries happen on the football field: the Univ. of Virginia supervises a project to simulate player impacts with modified crash-test mannequins.</p>\n<p>The research team <a href=\"https://www.playsmartplaysafe.com/focus-on-safety/advanced-technology/new-video-review-data-help-improve-designs-protective-equipment\" target=\"_blank\">compiled a review</a> of reported concussions that happened in NFL games. They shared data with helmet manufacturers, designers, entrepreneurs, universities to think-tank novel designs for protective gear.</p>\n<p>Based on those results, the NFL <a href=\"https://www.playsmartplaysafe.com/newsroom/statements/transcript-media-availability-dr-allen-sills-jeff-miller-march-1-2019\" target=\"_blank\">changed the kick-off rule</a> &#8212; this decreased reported concussions by 38 % on kick-off plays, compared to the prior 3-year average.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft  wp-image-334057 noshadow\" title=\"art - football player + geometric - no. 5\" src=\"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/art-football-player-+-geometric-no.-5.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"874\" /></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">The next 100 years.</span></p>\n<p>The NFL is trying to make football safer by:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>using digital models of players, their gear, and their movements</li>\n<li>changing game rules to reduce situations where the worst injuries happen</li>\n<li>designing better protective gear</li>\n<li>updating injury prevention protocols</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Looking ahead to the league’s next 100 years, the NFL said:</p>\n<p style=\"padding-left: 30px;\">We&#8217;re committed to re-imagining the future of football so that everybody wins &#8212; players, coaches, clubs, and fans. Our research will learn about the human body and how injuries happen. That knowledge will reach far beyond football. As we look ahead to our next 100 seasons, we’re proud of this endeavor.</p>\n<p style=\"padding-left: 30px;\">&#8212; <em>NFL</em></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">by definition</span> | What is cloud computing?</p>\n<p>The service called cloud computing is the on-demand delivery of information technology (IT) resources over the web with pay-as-you-go pricing.</p>\n<p>Instead of buying, owning, and maintaining computer equipment such as physical data centers + servers, a customer can access hardware + software tech services &#8212; like computing power, storage, and data-bases &#8212; on an as-needed basis from a cloud provider.</p>\n<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft  wp-image-334041 noshadow\" e &#124; The indie pop group Ra Ra Riot","link":"http://www.kurzweilai.net/?p=205325","description":"<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft size-full wp-image-315089 noshadow\" title=\"photo - amplifier - no. 1\" src=\"http://www.kurzweilai.net/images/photo-amplifier-no.-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"370\" /></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; music &#8212;</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">album:</span> <em>Beta Love</em><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">song:</span> &#8220;Binary Mind&#8221;<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">group:</span> Ra Ra Riot<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">year:</span> 2013</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">watch</span> | &#8220;Binary Mind&#8221; • <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rYmA0UuW1dU\" target=\"_blank\">music video</a><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">listen</span> | &#8220;Binary Mind&#8221; • <a href=\"https://soundcloud.com/rarariot/binary-mind\" target=\"_blank\">song</a></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft  wp-image-315091 noshadow\" title=\"hande made - art - Ra Ra Riot - no. 2\" src=\"http://www.kurzweilai.net/images/hande-made-art-Ra-Ra-Riot-no.-2.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"428\" /></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">selected reading</span></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p>no. 1 |</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">broadcast:</span> NPR<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">series:</span> <em>All Things Considered</em><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">story title:</span> <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/sections/allsongs/2013/08/12/211337593/first-watch-ra-ra-riot-binary-mind\" target=\"_blank\">First Watch: Ra Ra Riot&#8217;s &#8220;Binary Mind&#8221;</a><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">author:</span> by Robin Hilton<br />\nread | story</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; excerpt  &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>Indie pop group Ra Ra Riot album<em> Beta Love</em> is steeped in science fiction and futurism: with robots, space &#8212; and on the song &#8220;Binary Mind&#8221; merging  humans with computers. In a music video for the song the heads of the band members playfully float and bob in a kaleidoscope digital landscape.</p>\n<p>Ra Ra Riot singer Wes Miles says &#8220;Binary Mind&#8221; was one of the first songs written for <em>Beta Love</em> and helped shape their album. Miles said: &#8220;It&#8217;s written from the viewpoint of a fiction version of futurist Ray Kurzweil.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;In the song he longs for his father. He&#8217;s trying to merge with a computer and become immortal by uploading into the web. He wants to make an avatar of his father who he misses. He is dealing with time.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The director for the music video of &#8220;Binary Mind&#8221; Cole Hannan took a textured approach. Hannan used photos he took of places and objects while walking around town. He filmed the band members singing while wearing green screen bibs to isolate their heads. Hannan said: &#8220;I started thinking about the concept of singularity. I wanted to make a story about a planet being created. Life on that planet popping up, that life assimilating with computers, and its new human-computer hybrid.&#8221;</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p>no. 2 |</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">group:</span> <a href=\"http://www.ghsstrings.com\" target=\"_blank\">GHS Strings</a><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">section:</span> <a href=\"http://www.ghsstrings.com/artists\" target=\"_blank\">Artists</a><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">artist profile:</span> <a href=\"http://www.ghsstrings.com/users/2452118\" target=\"_blank\">Ra Ra Riot</a><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">author:</span> by Michael Tedder<br />\nread | story</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; excerpt &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>The band re-created themselves on their album <em>Beta Love</em>: a collection of giddy pop songs and heady lyrics that pull inspiration from futurist Ray Kurzweil among others.</p>\n<p><em>question</em> &#8212;Tell me about your song  “Binary Mind”  from your album <em>Beta Love</em>. That song has a science fiction-as-emotional conflict metaphor.</p>\n<p><em>Wes Miles</em> &#8212; Well, that song is about Ray Kurzweil. We got into him at the end of our album <em>the Orchard.</em> I majored in physics in college and I’m into science. Mathieu was also really into that.</p>\n<p><em>Mathieu Santos </em>&#8212; I ordered the book <em>the Singularity Is Near</em> by Ray Kurzweil.</p>\n<p><em>Wes Miles &#8212; </em>It’s all about his math, estimating when humans and computers will become fully integrated. There’s a great documentary about him, exploring that idea &#8212; called <em>Transcendent Man.</em> So we got into him and his ideas. Watching the movie you realize one of his biggest hopes for singularity is to sort of re-create his father. He has boxes of his father’s documents and personal writings &#8212; he believes it will help him create a sort of avatar of his dad.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile he’s racing against time in his own way &#8212; because according to his theory, singularity happens at a certain time. So that’s the song: from his perspective, hoping when singularity happens he’ll be able to sync with his computer and create his father &#8212; basically bring his father back to life.</p>\n<p><em>question </em>&#8212; Seems opposite your mind-set where you guys are trying to give up control &#8212; he’s trying to have control over death. Reminds me of the song “Dying Is Fine&#8221; from your first album. <em>Beta Love</em> is an interesting phrase &#8212; there’s the idea of beta as an in-progress software program, not quite ready to go.</p>\n<p><em>Wes Miles </em>&#8212; The lyrics in the song encapsulate a lot of topics on the record. It’s about a beta version of an android discovering love. But listening to it and writing all the lyrics, it felt like it was representative of everything.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p>no. 3 |</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">publication:</span> <em>Pitchfork</em><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">section:</span> <a href=\"https://pitchfork.com/reviews/albums/\" target=\"_blank\">Reviews</a><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">story title</span>: Ra Ra Riot • <em>Beta Love</em><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">author:</span> by Harley Brown<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">read</span> | <a href=\"https://pitchfork.com/reviews/albums/17513-beta-love\" target=\"_blank\">story</a></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; excerpt &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>Along with a lyrical focus inspired by author Ray Kurzweil&#8217;s book <em>the Singularity Is Near</em>, Ra Ra Riot incorporated more keyboards and synthesizers into many of the songs on their album <em>Beta Love</em>.</p>\n<p>This new techie attitude is a change for a band known mostly for one thing. The album peaks during the drums on &#8220;Binary Mind&#8221; &#8212; the songs that speaks about Ray Kurzweil&#8217;s idea of trans-humanism:</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p>no. 4 |</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">broadcast:</span> MTV<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">department.:</span> <a href=\"http://www.mtv.com/news/\" target=\"_blank\">News</a><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">section:</span> <a href=\"http://www.mtv.com/news/music/\" target=\"_blank\">Music</a><br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">story title:</span> 5 ways William Gibson + Ray Kurzweil influence Ra Ra Riot&#8217;s new album<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ff9900;\">author:</span> by Kory Grow<br />\n<span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">read</span> | <a href=\"http://www.mtv.com/news/2698147/ra-ra-riot-beta-love-william-gibson\" target=\"_blank\">story</a></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p>no. 5 |</p>\n<p>STORY</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img style=' float: left; Ray Kurzweil<br />\nfolder: daily blog &#8212; a + e</p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">[ end of file ]</span></p>\n","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sun, 01 Dec 2019 06:00:05 +0000","feedId":11321,"bgimg":"http://www.kurzweilai.net/images/photo-amplifier-no.-1.png","linkMd5":"51b6238bd6a9f0d0f1ec9bb300e24dbe","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn37@2020_4/2020/08/25/01-22-14-020_3eab49764614c704.webp","destWidth":1424,"destHeight":776,"sourceBytes":1921788,"destBytes":73400,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://www.kurzweilai.net/images/photo-amplifier-no.-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn37@2020_4/2020/08/25/01-22-14-020_3eab49764614c704.webp","http://www.kurzweilai.net/images/hande-made-art-Ra-Ra-Riot-no.-2.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn53@2020_6/2020/08/25/01-22-39-291_366050dd2db8b684.webp","http://www.kurzweilai.net/images/musician-Ra-Ra-Riot-no.-2.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn99@2020_4/2020/08/25/01-22-32-530_4296a47b6c0584c5.webp","http://www.kurzweilai.net/images/story-brand-Arts-+-Crafts-no.-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn97@2020_1/2020/08/25/01-22-31-988_8de2c08768ceafdc.webp","http://www.kurzweilai.net/images/story-brand-Barsuk-Records-no.-2.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn88@2020_2/2020/08/25/01-22-36-163_00cc51cb06151b99.webp","http://www.kurzweilai.net/images/musician-Ra-Ra-Riot-no.-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn68@2020_1/2020/08/25/01-22-30-065_3aa735af495821c9.webp","http://www.kurzweilai.net/images/story-brand-Barsuk-Records-no.-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn47@2020_5/2020/08/25/01-22-35-455_40080a7b23a4e682.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598318532656},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:22:12","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:22:12","title":"mailbox &#124; Are you worried about climate change?","link":"https://www.kurzweilai.net/?p=329845","description":"<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft  wp-image-334441 noshadow\" title=\"photo - mailbox + wall - no. 1\" src=\"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/photo-mailbox-+-wall-no.-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"525\" /></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<table class=\"pastel full\">\n<colgroup>\n<col style=\"width: 30%;\" />\n<col /> </colgroup>\n<thead>\n<tr>\n<th style=\"text-align: left;\" scope=\"col\" height=\"14\"></th>\n<th style=\"text-align: left;\" scope=\"col\"></th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td>topic</td>\n<td>Are you worried about climate change?</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>year</td>\n<td>2019</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; letter &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>Dear Ray,</p>\n<p>I&#8217;ve been a follower of your work since the late 1990s. Your optimism has always been a breath of fresh air. Unfortunately, while you&#8217;ve eloquently explained the principal of accelerating returns &#8212; Earth is undergoing non-intuitive systemic changes.</p>\n<p>In a 2011 interview you explained why you weren&#8217;t worried about climate change &#8212; but in that same year, a severe drought drove people in the country of Syria into a horrible humanitarian crisis that continues today.</p>\n<p>Now, climate change is exacerbating the conflict between the countries of Saudi Arabia + Yemen &#8212; and immigration issues in Central America due to water scarcity.</p>\n<p>Please help us fight climate change by lending your voice to the public discussion &#8212; and your mind for problem solving. I believe if you temper your previous level of optimism with a renewed look at the sobering reality we face, many people would listen. They&#8217;d respect your re-evaluation of our future.</p>\n<p>I don&#8217;t think facing the grim realities of the climate crisis &#8212; the 60-something feedback loops, and inevitable socio-political conflicts &#8212; would defeat your optimism. Because it&#8217;s simply part of who you are, and we need that right now. We need people who can see the urgent climate crisis for the threat it really is to human civilization &#8212; and still inspire a movement to fight its devastating impact.</p>\n<p>I&#8217;m not representing a specific advocacy group &#8212; I&#8217;m not affiliated with any activist organization. I&#8217;m just a concerned Earthling who&#8217;s also your fan. Thanks you for reading &#8212; and for all the inventions + insights over the years.</p>\n<p>&#8212; <em>Tom</em></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><img style=' float: left; padding: 4px; margin: 0 7px 2px 0;'  class=\"alignleft  wp-image-329859 noshadow\" title=\"photo - envelope - no. 1\" src=\"https://www.kurzweilai.net/images/photo-envelope-no.-11.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"486\" /></p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; letter &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>Dear Tom,</p>\n<p>Hello and thanks for writing.</p>\n<p>You make some good points. As I&#8217;ll explain in my upcoming book titled <em>The Singularity Is Nearer</em>, the world is moving in the right direction on all of the issues that affect human well-being.</p>\n<p>But that doesn&#8217;t mean it&#8217;s perfect &#8212; or that bad things won’t happen. The same thing is happening with renewable energy. summary &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>The Breakthrough of the Year is an annual award made by the editors of the AAAS journal<em> Science &#8212; </em>for the most significant development in scientific research. It is widely considered one of the highest distinctions in science.</p>\n<p>The award was founded in year 1989 &#8212; originally called Molecule of the Year. The award name was changed in year 1996 to Breakthrough of the Year. It&#8217;s given to a novel discovery that makes headway in solving a long-standing problem &#8212; and is interesting to a wide range of people.</p>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: Empowered by:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>world class faculty</li>\n<li>trail-blazing practitioners</li>\n<li>global network partners</li>\n<li>impact start-ups</li>\n<li>engaged alumni</li>\n</ul>\n<hr class=\"dotted\" />\n<p><span style=\"color: #ffaa00;\">&#8212; welcome letter &#8212;</span></p>\n<p>Welcome to Exponential Medicine,</p>\n<p>On behalf of the Singularity University team, and the incredible faculty who have come together for Exponential Medicine, I’m thrilled and grateful to have you join us.</p>\n<p>Whether you&#8217;re a clinician, patient, technologist &#8212; from pharma, payor, medical device, or investor worlds &#8212; I appreciate the diverse spirit of innovation + collaboration you bring to the event. Our audience has vast, varied experience and ideas.
